  function DOMTokenListSupports(tokenList, token) {
    if (!tokenList || !tokenList.supports) {
      return false;
    }
    try {
      return tokenList.supports(token);
    } catch (e) {
      if (e instanceof TypeError) {
        console.log('The DOMTokenList doesn\'t have a supported tokens list.', e);
      } else {
        console.error('That shouldn\'t have happened.', e);
      }
    }
  };

  function loadAdLib(script) {
    if (!window.__AdLib) {
      
        var domainEnv = '.vice.com';
      
      var adLibScript = document.createElement('script');
      adLibScript.src = script;
      adLibScript.id = 'ad-lib';
      adLibScript.onload = () => {
        if (window.__AdLib) {
          window.__AdLib.env = 'production';
          window.__AdLib.template = 'article';
          window.__AdLib.site = 'vice';
          window.__AdLib.brand = 'vice';
          window.__AdLib.domain = domainEnv;
          window.__AdLib.init();
        }
      }
      adLibScript.onerror = (e) => {
        console.error('Ad-Lib could not load it\'s script.', e);
      }
      document.head.appendChild(adLibScript);
    }
  }

  var linkSupportsPreload = DOMTokenListSupports(document.createElement('link').relList, 'preload');

  if (!linkSupportsPreload) {
    console.log('linkSupportsPreload not supported!');
    loadAdLib('https://vice-web-statics-cdn.vice.com/vendor/ad-lib/v2.3.1/vice-ad-lib.js');
  }
</script>

When I was 18, I thought Id learn maybe five languages, minimum, by the time I was 30. Now I just about cope with one (and a half, if you count my terrible Mandarin). When I was 21, I thought Id get buff by the time I was 27. Well, 27 came and went with me working out exactly as little as I did when I was 21.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESo, now, I'm starting to get the point of resolutions as I accelerate ever-faster towards decrepitude. Why \u003Ci\u003Enot\u003C\u002Fi\u003E give yourself a little annual motivation shot to do the things that you always thought youd get around to? As Im such a newbie to this, I figured that I may as well give myself an immersive primer on what itd be like to live a new life based around makingcommitting tomy New Years resolutions. This is how I ended up doing all 10 of the most common New Years resolutions in a week. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Ch2\u003E Exercise more (38 percent)\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAccording to \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.telegraph.co.uk\u002Fhealth-fitness\u002Fbody\u002Fcommon-new-years-resolutions-stick\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EComRes\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, 38 percent of British adults make a solemn vow to exercise more in the new year. For 24, I can exercise as much as my hearts desire or till my heart explodes, whichever comes first.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EOn the first day of my resolution, I wake up at 9 AM and fail to go to the gym. On the second day, I finally drag my ass in for a class that promises to be a hybrid full-body workout combining high-intensity, high-impact cardio achieving high fat loss and small muscle isolations and and isometric holds.\" I sweat so much that my face continues sweating, even after I leave the shower, and Im exhausted all day at work. Is thisfitness?\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBy the end of the week, Ive exercised four times, including three days in a row. class=\"article__image-caption\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \u003Ch2\u003E Lose weight (33 percent)\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E \u003Cp\u003ERead my lips: I have no desire to lose weight. Instead, what I desire in winter is to be wrapped in a warm and huggable layer of flesh, like a human mochi ball or an especially plump dumpling. Also, I dont own a bathroom scale. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAt this time of year, the media is awash with new diet crazes which often have no scientific backing. Some can be unsafe ,so many diet resolutions are often not sensible anyway, says Kiri Elliott, a lecturer in dietetics at Birmingham City University. New Years resolutions around food are often related to weight loss, and as desired results arent instant, many lose motivation to continue.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"article__embed article__embed--vice\" data-related-article=\"true\"\u003E\u003Ciframe src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fbroadly.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Fembed\u002Farticle\u002F3k8nm8\u002Fwhy-your-new-years-resolutions-are-doomed-to-fail?utm_source=stylizedembed_broadly.vice.com&amp;utm_campaign=mbydja&amp;site=broadly\" frameborder=\"0\" style=\"border:0px none;margin:0px;\" allowfullscreen=\"\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EJust because I think this resolution is a waste of time that doesnt mean Im not going to do this resolution. Since I cant weigh myself, I do the next-best thingI measure myself around the waist and hips with some tape. I figure that in four exercise classes time, I will almost definitely have lost an inch or two. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003ETurns out this is absolutely bogus! By the end of the week, I display no discernible weight loss around either my waist or my hips. In fact, I may even have put on some weight, because I started my period during the week and have started to bloat into the plump dumpling form I prefer this time of year, anyway.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003ELove tells me that viewing exercise as a route to weight loss isnt the best approach: This is not about losing weight; it is building a way of living that will keep you healthy and active for a long, long time. Given that my weight fluctuates so much, Im tempted to agree. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article__media\"\u003E\u003Cpicture class=\"article__image\"\u003E\u003Csource media=\"(max-width: class=\"article__image-caption\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \u003Ch2\u003E Eat more healthily (32 percent)\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E \u003Cp\u003EOn the first day of my resolutions, I virtuously get a lemongrass chicken salad for lunch. By about 4 PM, Ive caved and eaten my coworkers emergency bowl of Skittles. This rollercoaster continues at dinner, when I order a macrobiotic bowl that tastes like something yakked up from a fermented cow stomach and end up eating the rest of my friends fries. After departing the restaurant, I am so angered by my poor food choices that I walk directly into a nearby Taiwanese dessert caf and eat a brioche ice cream sandwich. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EMany New Years resolutions are actually quite radical, explains Elliott. Rather than small manageable steps towards healthier eating, they involve drastic changes which are hugely difficult to adhere to.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"article__embed article__embed--vice\" data-related-article=\"true\"\u003E\u003Ciframe src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fbroadly.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Fembed\u002Farticle\u002Fzmdqze\u002Fdoes-sex-count-as-exercise?utm_source=stylizedembed_broadly.vice.com&amp;utm_campaign=mbydja&amp;site=broadly\" frameborder=\"0\" style=\"border:0px none;margin:0px;\" allowfullscreen=\"\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIts much better to break a resolution right down into one or two 'SMART' [specific, measurable, achievable, realistic, and timely] goals, which are well-thought-out and -planned, she adds. For example, rather than aiming to shed a stone by following the latest 600kcal detox diet, it would be better to consider overall health and perhaps choose to switch one unhealthy snack per day to one healthy snack such as a piece of fruit, and to add an extra half hour of exercise into my week. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EThis is great advice which I absolutely dont adhere to over the course of the week. In fact, the command to eat healthy appears to have flipped some kind of switch in my brain, so I actually eat even more shittily than I did before. It doesnt help that my sudden upswing in exercise means that Im suddenly ravenously hungry all the time. During a mid-afternoon lull, I eat a whole bag of potato chips and then a banana in a guilty attempt to compensate. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBy the end of the week, Im eating instant ramen and microwaving leftover cauliflower cheese in a plastic takeaway box. The one good thing is that Ive cut down on my Diet Coke consumption. Im not a dietician, but I think that the macrobiotic bowl got the whole thing off to a bad start. Trying to limit my own natural food consumptionI would never ordinarily order something like itset myself up for failure. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article__media\"\u003E\u003Cpicture class=\"article__image-caption\"\u003EPhoto by Zing Tsjeng.\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \u003Ch2\u003E Take a more active approach to health (15 percent) \u003C\u002Fh2\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAfter this much exercise, I have no desire to do any more physical activity. Instead, I decide to do something good for my health that Ive been putting off for ages: I visit a dentist. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EMy last appointment was sometime in 2016 (dont judge me), so this is visit is long overdue. As I settle into the dentist's chair, Im suddenly plagued by flashbacks of terrible dentist visits from my childhood, including having a suffocating wad of orthodontic cement shoved in my mouth so I could mold a retainer for my lispy underbite. This, I realize, is whats been preventing me from booking a dentist appointment. As a grown-up, why would I willingly revisit a place I associate with memories that still make me physically gag? \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"article__embed article__embed--vice\" data-related-article=\"true\"\u003E\u003Ciframe src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fbroadly.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Fembed\u002Farticle\u002Fd3bk5v\u002Femotional-baggage-worst-habit-zodiac-sign-2018-horoscope?utm_source=stylizedembed_broadly.vice.com&amp;utm_campaign=mbydja&amp;site=broadly\" frameborder=\"0\" style=\"border:0px none;margin:0px;\" allowfullscreen=\"\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EHow often do you change your toothbrush? my new dentist asks. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EI hazard a guess: Uhevery four to six months? There is a long pause. You should change it every two to three months, he tells me, a note of sadness in his voice. I imagine how hard it must be for dentists. Theirs is not the glamorous job of heart surgeons; you cant imagine one ever being called McDreamy or starring in a beloved 14-season long TV drama scripted by Shonda Rhimes. Theyre really not the bogeymen that I grew up believing they were. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBy the time my dentist tells me Ive got some signs of early gum disease (great), happily takes a photo of me lying in his chair, and schedules me in for a cleanup later in January, Ive warmed to this resolution. Visiting the dentist honestly wasnt that bad, and Ive potentially averted a much more serious health crisis. Plus, thanks to the National Health Service, it only cost me 21.60 for a first-time checkup. something less extra for this resolution, like learn a new language, but I figure that 2019 calls for extreme measures. Who knows what will happen after Brexit? By July, I could be fending off survivalists for the last tin of baked beans in an abandoned supermarket in Walton-Upon-Thames. Ive got to prepare for the worst. Hence: axe throwing. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EWhistle Punks bills itself as one of the only places in the UK where you can learn to hurl axes with pinpoint accuracy, so I head down to their outpost in South London to try some urban axe throwing. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EJames Bidgood, the head of marketing at Whistle Punks, tells me that throwing axes is actually easier than it looks. You dont have to be strong to do it, he says. Its all about using your body and getting your rhythm. He tells me to perish the thought of axe throwing being the reserve of huge, barrel-chested men in lumberjack shirts. You do get macho guys in here to chuck axes as hard as they can, but they usually embarrass themselves.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article__media\"\u003E\u003Cpicture of person who takes bubble baths or invests in skincare as acts of self-care (no offense to those who doI just find baths kind of boring). Can I do something easy that doesnt involve bankrupting myself on SK-II sheet masks? \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"article__embed article__embed--vice\" data-related-article=\"true\"\u003E\u003Ciframe src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fbroadly.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Fembed\u002Farticle\u002Fywejyg\u002Fi-did-everything-millennials-accused-killing?utm_source=stylizedembed_broadly.vice.com&amp;utm_campaign=mbydja&amp;site=broadly\" frameborder=\"0\" style=\"border:0px none;margin:0px;\" allowfullscreen=\"\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EI turn to Samata Angel, a fashion and media entrepreneur who is the author of \u003Ci\u003E THE TRIBE Empowerment Journal, \u003C\u002Fi\u003Ea new book that encourages women to write down one thing they celebrate about themselves every day. Journalling is a great way to steer your inner narrative. We share so much publicly and online these days, she says. I like the idea of taking that control back. We are entitled to feel proud of ourselves and are allowed to celebrate our achievements without the public applause. It's a non-judgmental place to be heard.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EI forget to journal on my first day and retrospectively do it on my laptop the next afternoon. Im not doing so great at this, clearly. Something about living in the UKthe land of crippling self-awareness thinly plastered over by a sense of ironyhas made me unable to journal sincerely. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EBy the end of the week, something has happened that does make me feel a little proud of myself. A guy outside a pub with his mate calls me a Chinese bitch, and I simply and efficiently flip them off and keep walking. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EThis is such an upgrade to how Ive previously responded (think: immediate and undignified tears) that Im actually pretty proud of myself. Unfortunately, Im also so angry about it that I also end up tweeting about it. By the end of the week, Ive had half a glass of wine and a beer in total. I dont feel like Ive missed out on drinking at all. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EThe only time I am tempted is when I head to the pub to catch up with an old work friend I havent seen in ages, and she invites two of her friends along. Being the odd one out with a pint of lime soda almost makes me order a vodka tonic, but luckily I have to head off before the social awkwardness almost torpedoes my resolution. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAt the end of the week, I find myself in a gay bar drinking another pint of lime soda and talking to someone whos in recovery. The best thing to do, they advise me, is to not tell anyone youre not drinking. class=\"article__image-caption\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \u003Ch2\u003E Stop smoking (9 percent)\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E \u003Cp\u003EI dont smoke (which is what I tell my mom), but I do smoke socially (which I dont tell her). If I see a friend smoking when Im bored or one or two drinks down, I will inevitably pester them for a cigarette. But this cant be \u003Ci\u003Ethat\u003C\u002Fi\u003E bad for me, right? \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EDr. Elena Touroni, a consultant psychologist and cofounder and chief operating officer of My Online Therapy, disagrees: You might not be physically addicted to smoking, but you might have developed a psychological addiction. This means that your brain often gives the message that, in order to have more fun when you are socializing, you need to smoke. Over time, this becomes an association and a learned behavior, so you are likely to have urges to smoke when you are in that situation.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"article__embed article__embed--vice\" data-related-article=\"true\"\u003E\u003Ciframe src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fbroadly.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Fembed\u002Farticle\u002Fevgxee\u002Fmy-14-year-old-cousin-taught-me-how-to-be-a-cool-teen?utm_source=stylizedembed_broadly.vice.com&amp;utm_campaign=mbydja&amp;site=broadly\" frameborder=\"0\" style=\"border:0px none;margin:0px;\" allowfullscreen=\"\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIm out at a Christmas party or a social event almost every night this week, which means an infinite number of possibilities to beg people for smokes. Touroni suggests having a game plan: Visualize being in the social situation in advance of time. Rehearse how you might manage it differently. What do you say when others invite you outside the pub or the club for a smoke? Think clearly about how you can say no, what explanation you offer, and how you might feel afterwards.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp class=\"article__blockquote\"\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fconfirmsubscription.com\u002Fh\u002Fi\u002FDC735105D83847D9\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EFor More Stories Like This, Sign Up for Our Newsletter\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\"Think about all the feelings that might make you want to join them. Are you worried about feeling left out of the group? Are you worried you might have less fun? Whatever it is, consider all the reasons you want to give up, and next time you are in that situation try to bring them readily to mind.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003ESadly, this doesnt quite work for me. It takes me about two hours before I cave and ask someone at the aforementioned gay bar for a cigarette. But I havent smoked in a while, and as the nicotine unpleasantly hits sober me, unaided by the boozy fugue I usually imbibe one in, Im kind of wondering why I even bothered in the first place. Maybe these cancerous tar sticks arebad? \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Ch2\u003E Other (1 percent)\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E \u003Cp\u003EOnly one percent of the British public has a resolution that doesnt fall into the previous nine Ive tried out, so heres mine: Im never doing another New Year's resolution again. Or, Im never going to try doing almost all of them at once because its impossible to effectively fulfill all of them at one go. Heres my advice: If you are keen on the idea of setting some 2019 goals, go easy on yourself, because you will fuck up. Dont set yourself impossible targets, like trying to go to the gym every day or swapping all your meals for macrobiotic bowls. Finally, congratulate yourself on actually making it to 2019you did good just surviving 2018. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EOh! long-form-v2--center m-t-4--xs m-b-6--xs"></div><p class="long-form-v2__credit long-form-v2--center ff--accent lh--headline size--6 uppercased">Photo by Bex Wade.</p><div class="article-keep-reading"><div class="article-keep-reading__children-container m-t-5--xs" tabindex="-1"><div data-type="body-text" class="article__body article__body dsp-block-xx ff--body-article size--article lh--body"><p class="article__text--dropcap">I have never once made a New Year's resolution, but as I get older, the more I feel like time is running out on me. When I was 18, I thought Id learn maybe five languages, minimum, by the time I was 30. Now I just about cope with one (and a half, if you count my terrible Mandarin). When I was 21, I thought Id get buff by the time I was 27. Well, 27 came and went with me working out exactly as little as I did when I was 21.<br></p> <div class="ad-unit__container__container"><div class="article-iac__wrapper"></div></div><p>So, now, I'm starting to get the point of resolutions as I accelerate ever-faster towards decrepitude. Why <i>not</i> give yourself a little annual motivation shot to do the things that you always thought youd get around to? As Im such a newbie to this, I figured that I may as well give myself an immersive primer on what itd be like to live a new life based around makingcommitting tomy New Years resolutions. This is how I ended up doing all 10 of the most common New Years resolutions in a week. </p> <h2> Exercise more (38 percent)</h2> <p>According to <a href="https://www.telegraph.co.uk/health-fitness/body/common-new-years-resolutions-stick/" target="_blank">ComRes</a>, 38 percent of British adults make a solemn vow to exercise more in the new year. Fortunately, a gym near my office does a seven-day all-you-can-exercise deal. For 24, I can exercise as much as my hearts desire or till my heart explodes, whichever comes first.</p> <p>On the first day of my resolution, I wake up at 9 AM and fail to go to the gym. On the second day, I finally drag my ass in for a class that promises to be a hybrid full-body workout combining high-intensity, high-impact cardio achieving high fat loss and small muscle isolations and and isometric holds." I sweat so much that my face continues sweating, even after I leave the shower, and Im exhausted all day at work. Is thisfitness?</p><p>By the end of the week, Ive exercised four times, including three days in a row. I feel marginally fitter (I can do mountain climbers now!), but am also finding it increasingly difficult to fathom a life in which I get up at 7 AM and do this every day of the week.</p><div Wade.</div></div> <p>London Loves Fitness founder and personal trainer Roger Love advises me to start simpler: If you are doing it alone, start small. Don't feel you have to do the perfect, super-complicated work-out. Do something simplea brisk walk, or some jumping jacks, squats, or press-ups. Undoubtedly, it will not be the workout you are still doing in the spring, but it will get you started.<br></p> <p>Hes not surprised when I tell him that Im finding it hard to consistently work out. Remember: It does not have to be perfect. If you have a bad day, it doesn't need to lead to a bad week. You are not a robot; you will have bad days and make mistakes. Dust yourself off and go again. Remind yourself why you started training.</p> <div class="ad-unit__container__container"><div class="article-iac__wrapper"></div></div><p>Good pointI havent actually set myself an aim for why Ive actually started going to the gym. Do I want to be stronger? Bench press my own weight? Be able to handle myself in a fight? Maybe its best to see working out as a means to an end, rather than an end in itself.</p><div class="article__media"><picture class="article__image"><source media="(max-width: 25em)" srcset="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" alt="Zing Tsjeng outside a gym" class="col-12-xs" data-src="https://video-images.vice.com/_uncategorized/1545802807342-Broadly-10-New-Years-Resolutions-Photo-Bex-Wade-28.jpeg"></picture><div class="article__image-caption"></div></div> <h2> Lose weight (33 percent)</h2> <p>Read my lips: I have no desire to lose weight. Instead, what I desire in winter is to be wrapped in a warm and huggable layer of flesh, like a human mochi ball or an especially plump dumpling. Also, I dont own a bathroom scale. </p> <p>At this time of year, the media is awash with new diet crazes which often have no scientific backing. Some can be unsafe ,so many diet resolutions are often not sensible anyway, says Kiri Elliott, a lecturer in dietetics at Birmingham City University. New Years resolutions around food are often related to weight loss, and as desired results arent instant, many lose motivation to continue.</p> <div class="article__embed article__embed--vice" data-related-article="true"><iframe src="https://broadly.vice.com/en_us/embed/article/3k8nm8/why-your-new-years-resolutions-are-doomed-to-fail?utm_source=stylizedembed_broadly.vice.com&amp;utm_campaign=mbydja&amp;site=broadly" frameborder="0" style="border:0px none;margin:0px;" allowfullscreen=""></iframe></div><p>Just because I think this resolution is a waste of time that doesnt mean Im not going to do this resolution. Since I cant weigh myself, I do the next-best thingI measure myself around the waist and hips with some tape. I figure that in four exercise classes time, I will almost definitely have lost an inch or two. </p> <p>Turns out this is absolutely bogus! By the end of the week, I display no discernible weight loss around either my waist or my hips. In fact, I may even have put on some weight, because I started my period during the week and have started to bloat into the plump dumpling form I prefer this time of year, anyway.</p> <div class="ad-unit__container__container"><div class="article-iac__wrapper"></div></div><p>Love tells me that viewing exercise as a route to weight loss isnt the best approach: This is not about losing weight; it is building a way of living that will keep you healthy and active for a long, long time. Given that my weight fluctuates so much, Im tempted to agree. </p><div class="article__media"><picture class="article__image"><source media="(max-width: 25em)" srcset="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" data-srcset="https://video-images.vice.com/_uncategorized/1545802871181-Broadly-10-New-Years-Resolutions-Photo-Bex-Wade-23.jpeg?resize=400:*, srcset="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" srcset="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" https://video-images.vice.com/_uncategorized/1545802871181-Broadly-10-New-Years-Resolutions-Photo-Bex-Wade-23.jpeg?resize=1575:* 2x"><source media="(min-width: 65.625em)" srcset="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" data-srcset="https://video-images.vice.com/_uncategorized/1545802871181-Broadly-10-New-Years-Resolutions-Photo-Bex-Wade-23.jpeg?resize=1050:*, https://video-images.vice.com/_uncategorized/1545802871181-Broadly-10-New-Years-Resolutions-Photo-Bex-Wade-23.jpeg?resize=1575:* 2x"><img src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" alt="Zing Tsjeng eating a salad" class="col-12-xs" data-src="https://video-images.vice.com/_uncategorized/1545802871181-Broadly-10-New-Years-Resolutions-Photo-Bex-Wade-23.jpeg"></picture><div class="article__image-caption"></div></div> <h2> Eat more healthily (32 percent)</h2> <p>On the first day of my resolutions, I virtuously get a lemongrass chicken salad for lunch. By about 4 PM, Ive caved and eaten my coworkers emergency bowl of Skittles. This rollercoaster continues at dinner, when I order a macrobiotic bowl that tastes like something yakked up from a fermented cow stomach and end up eating the rest of my friends fries. After departing the restaurant, I am so angered by my poor food choices that I walk directly into a nearby Taiwanese dessert caf and eat a brioche ice cream sandwich. </p> <p>Many New Years resolutions are actually quite radical, explains Elliott. Rather than small manageable steps towards healthier eating, they involve drastic changes which are hugely difficult to adhere to.</p> <div class="article__embed article__embed--vice" data-related-article="true"><iframe src="https://broadly.vice.com/en_us/embed/article/zmdqze/does-sex-count-as-exercise?utm_source=stylizedembed_broadly.vice.com&amp;utm_campaign=mbydja&amp;site=broadly" frameborder="0" style="border:0px none;margin:0px;" allowfullscreen=""></iframe></div><p>Its much better to break a resolution right down into one or two 'SMART' [specific, measurable, achievable, realistic, and timely] goals, which are well-thought-out and -planned, she adds. For example, rather than aiming to shed a stone by following the latest 600kcal detox diet, it would be better to consider overall health and perhaps choose to switch one unhealthy snack per day to one healthy snack such as a piece of fruit, and to add an extra half hour of exercise into my week. </p> <p>This is great advice which I absolutely dont adhere to over the course of the week. In fact, the command to eat healthy appears to have flipped some kind of switch in my brain, so I actually eat even more shittily than I did before. It doesnt help that my sudden upswing in exercise means that Im suddenly ravenously hungry all the time. During a mid-afternoon lull, I eat a whole bag of potato chips and then a banana in a guilty attempt to compensate. </p> <div class="ad-unit__container__container"><div class="article-iac__wrapper"></div></div><p>By the end of the week, Im eating instant ramen and microwaving leftover cauliflower cheese in a plastic takeaway box. The one good thing is that Ive cut down on my Diet Coke consumption. Im not a dietician, but I think that the macrobiotic bowl got the whole thing off to a bad start. Trying to limit my own natural food consumptionI would never ordinarily order something like itset myself up for failure. </p><div class="article__media"><picture class="article__image"><source media="(max-width: 25em)" srcset="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" srcset="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" data-srcset="https://video-images.vice.com/_uncategorized/1545803416906-MVIMG_20181221_111857.jpeg?resize=850:*, dentist" class="col-12-xs" data-src="https://video-images.vice.com/_uncategorized/1545803416906-MVIMG_20181221_111857.jpeg"></picture><div class="article__image-caption">Photo by Zing Tsjeng.</div></div> <h2> Take a more active approach to health (15 percent) </h2> <p>After this much exercise, I have no desire to do any more physical activity. Instead, I decide to do something good for my health that Ive been putting off for ages: I visit a dentist. </p> <p>My last appointment was sometime in 2016 (dont judge me), so this is visit is long overdue. As I settle into the dentist's chair, Im suddenly plagued by flashbacks of terrible dentist visits from my childhood, including having a suffocating wad of orthodontic cement shoved in my mouth so I could mold a retainer for my lispy underbite. This, I realize, is whats been preventing me from booking a dentist appointment. As a grown-up, why would I willingly revisit a place I associate with memories that still make me physically gag? </p> <div class="article__embed article__embed--vice" data-related-article="true"><iframe src="https://broadly.vice.com/en_us/embed/article/d3bk5v/emotional-baggage-worst-habit-zodiac-sign-2018-horoscope?utm_source=stylizedembed_broadly.vice.com&amp;utm_campaign=mbydja&amp;site=broadly" frameborder="0" style="border:0px none;margin:0px;" allowfullscreen=""></iframe></div><p>How often do you change your toothbrush? my new dentist asks. </p> <p>I hazard a guess: Uhevery four to six months? There is a long pause. You should change it every two to three months, he tells me, a note of sadness in his voice. I imagine how hard it must be for dentists. Theirs is not the glamorous job of heart surgeons; you cant imagine one ever being called McDreamy or starring in a beloved 14-season long TV drama scripted by Shonda Rhimes. Theyre really not the bogeymen that I grew up believing they were. </p> <div class="ad-unit__container__container"><div class="article-iac__wrapper"></div></div><p>By the time my dentist tells me Ive got some signs of early gum disease (great), happily takes a photo of me lying in his chair, and schedules me in for a cleanup later in January, Ive warmed to this resolution. Visiting the dentist honestly wasnt that bad, and Ive potentially averted a much more serious health crisis. Plus, thanks to the National Health Service, it only cost me 21.60 for a first-time checkup. Socialismand dentistryworks! </p><div class="article__media"><picture class="article__image"><source media="(max-width: 25em)" srcset="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" skill or hobby (15 percent) </h2> <p>I could definitely have done something less extra for this resolution, like learn a new language, but I figure that 2019 calls for extreme measures. Who knows what will happen after Brexit? By July, I could be fending off survivalists for the last tin of baked beans in an abandoned supermarket in Walton-Upon-Thames. Ive got to prepare for the worst. Hence: axe throwing. </p> <p>Whistle Punks bills itself as one of the only places in the UK where you can learn to hurl axes with pinpoint accuracy, so I head down to their outpost in South London to try some urban axe throwing. </p> <p>James Bidgood, the head of marketing at Whistle Punks, tells me that throwing axes is actually easier than it looks. You dont have to be strong to do it, he says. Its all about using your body and getting your rhythm. He tells me to perish the thought of axe throwing being the reserve of huge, barrel-chested men in lumberjack shirts. You do get macho guys in here to chuck axes as hard as they can, but they usually embarrass themselves.</p><div class="article__media"><picture class="article__image"><source media="(max-width: 25em)" srcset="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" instructor, Yamthe, beckons me into one of the training alleys. Theyre decked out like baseball batting cages, with a bullseye carved into a sturdy sheet of wood at the end of it. My first couple of axes go terribly and bounce off the target, but then I manage to find my sweet spotits all about leaning into the momentum of your swing, as opposed to hurling it as hard as you can. My axe scythes through the air and implants itself with a satisfying thwack near the bullseye. Im a natural! </p> <p>My next few axes bounce harmlessly off the wood. Maybe not. We do get a lot of new customers in January as a New Year thing, Bidgood says. It looks like it may take more than a single session for me to get lucky again, so maybe I should have stuck to learning Spanish.</p><div class="article__media"><picture class="article__image"><source time on personal well-being (12 percent) </h2> <p>I am not the kind of person who takes bubble baths or invests in skincare as acts of self-care (no offense to those who doI just find baths kind of boring). Can I do something easy that doesnt involve bankrupting myself on SK-II sheet masks? </p> <div class="article__embed article__embed--vice" data-related-article="true"><iframe src="https://broadly.vice.com/en_us/embed/article/ywejyg/i-did-everything-millennials-accused-killing?utm_source=stylizedembed_broadly.vice.com&amp;utm_campaign=mbydja&amp;site=broadly" frameborder="0" style="border:0px none;margin:0px;" allowfullscreen=""></iframe></div><p>I turn to Samata Angel, a fashion and media entrepreneur who is the author of <i> THE TRIBE Empowerment Journal, </i>a new book that encourages women to write down one thing they celebrate about themselves every day. Journalling is a great way to steer your inner narrative. We share so much publicly and online these days, she says. I like the idea of taking that control back. We are entitled to feel proud of ourselves and are allowed to celebrate our achievements without the public applause. It's a non-judgmental place to be heard.</p> <div class="ad-unit__container__container"><div class="article-iac__wrapper"></div></div><p>I forget to journal on my first day and retrospectively do it on my laptop the next afternoon. Proud of: only drinking half a glass of wine on Monday. Second day: Proud of: telling an coworker some office gossip from the Christmas party that made them almost choke with laughter. Im not doing so great at this, clearly. Something about living in the UKthe land of crippling self-awareness thinly plastered over by a sense of ironyhas made me unable to journal sincerely. </p> <p>By the end of the week, something has happened that does make me feel a little proud of myself. A guy outside a pub with his mate calls me a Chinese bitch, and I simply and efficiently flip them off and keep walking. </p> <p>This is such an upgrade to how Ive previously responded (think: immediate and undignified tears) that Im actually pretty proud of myself. Unfortunately, Im also so angry about it that I also end up tweeting about it. As far as more official journalling goes, I do feel pretty pleased with myself when I write down the words, Proud of: giving a racist man the finger.</p><div class="article__media"><picture class="article__image"><source media="(max-width: 25em)" srcset="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" time with family and friends (12 percent) </h2> <p>I breeze through this resolution, as Im seeing friends almost every other night this week. Who are these losers who cant find time in their lives for the people who matter most? Then I remember that I spent most of 2017 and 2018 in the dark cave of the British Library writing my book series, Forgotten Women, and I sober up. Sometimes, life and work do get in the way of hanging out with your nearest and dearest, but its always good to recalibrate. </p> <div class="ad-unit__container__container"><div class="article-iac__wrapper"></div></div><p>I text a friend to see what shes doing later in the week, and then cook dinner for 10 of my friends on the weekend. I realize I havent seen some of them in months. Even bettersome of them help me do the dishes. </p><div class="article__media"><picture class="article__image"><source media="(max-width: 25em)" srcset="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" data-src="https://video-images.vice.com/_uncategorized/1545803260115-Broadly-10-New-Years-Resolutions-Photo-Bex-Wade-10.jpeg"></picture><div class="article__image-caption"></div></div> <h2> Drink less alcohol (12 percent) </h2> <p>Im slightly surprised that only 12 percent of the population want to booze less, given that people around the world are <a href="https://www.ft.com/content/5b7fab74-47a2-11e7-8d27-59b4dd6296b8" target="_blank">actually drinking less</a> than they did before. Given that were heading towards the end of the Christmas party season, it seems like almost everyone has overindulged and is trying to cut back before heading home for the holidays. By the end of the week, Ive had half a glass of wine and a beer in total. I dont feel like Ive missed out on drinking at all. </p> <p>The only time I am tempted is when I head to the pub to catch up with an old work friend I havent seen in ages, and she invites two of her friends along. Being the odd one out with a pint of lime soda almost makes me order a vodka tonic, but luckily I have to head off before the social awkwardness almost torpedoes my resolution. </p> <p>At the end of the week, I find myself in a gay bar drinking another pint of lime soda and talking to someone whos in recovery. The best thing to do, they advise me, is to not tell anyone youre not drinking. Apparently, most people assume youre drinking exactly like them, and not disabusing them of this notion cuts down on awkwardness. </p><div class="article__media"><picture class="article__image"><source media="(max-width: 25em)" srcset="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" srcset="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" https://video-images.vice.com/_uncategorized/1545803301141-Broadly-10-New-Years-Resolutions-Photo-Bex-Wade-26.jpeg?resize=1275:* 2x"><source media="(max-width: 65.625em)" srcset="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" data-srcset="https://video-images.vice.com/_uncategorized/1545803301141-Broadly-10-New-Years-Resolutions-Photo-Bex-Wade-26.jpeg?resize=1050:*, https://video-images.vice.com/_uncategorized/1545803301141-Broadly-10-New-Years-Resolutions-Photo-Bex-Wade-26.jpeg?resize=1575:* 2x"><source media="(min-width: 65.625em)" srcset="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" data-srcset="https://video-images.vice.com/_uncategorized/1545803301141-Broadly-10-New-Years-Resolutions-Photo-Bex-Wade-26.jpeg?resize=1050:*, https://video-images.vice.com/_uncategorized/1545803301141-Broadly-10-New-Years-Resolutions-Photo-Bex-Wade-26.jpeg?resize=1575:* 2x"><img src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD/ACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=" alt="Zing Tsjeng putting cigarettes in the bin" class="col-12-xs" data-src="https://video-images.vice.com/_uncategorized/1545803301141-Broadly-10-New-Years-Resolutions-Photo-Bex-Wade-26.jpeg"></picture><div class="article__image-caption"></div></div> <h2> Stop smoking (9 percent)</h2> <p>I dont smoke (which is what I tell my mom), but I do smoke socially (which I dont tell her). If I see a friend smoking when Im bored or one or two drinks down, I will inevitably pester them for a cigarette. But this cant be <i>that</i> bad for me, right? </p> <div class="ad-unit__container__container"><div class="article-iac__wrapper"></div></div><p>Dr. Elena Touroni, a consultant psychologist and cofounder and chief operating officer of My Online Therapy, disagrees: You might not be physically addicted to smoking, but you might have developed a psychological addiction. This means that your brain often gives the message that, in order to have more fun when you are socializing, you need to smoke. Over time, this becomes an association and a learned behavior, so you are likely to have urges to smoke when you are in that situation.</p> <div class="article__embed article__embed--vice" data-related-article="true"><iframe src="https://broadly.vice.com/en_us/embed/article/evgxee/my-14-year-old-cousin-taught-me-how-to-be-a-cool-teen?utm_source=stylizedembed_broadly.vice.com&amp;utm_campaign=mbydja&amp;site=broadly" frameborder="0" style="border:0px none;margin:0px;" allowfullscreen=""></iframe></div><p>Im out at a Christmas party or a social event almost every night this week, which means an infinite number of possibilities to beg people for smokes. Touroni suggests having a game plan: Visualize being in the social situation in advance of time. Rehearse how you might manage it differently. What do you say when others invite you outside the pub or the club for a smoke? Think clearly about how you can say no, what explanation you offer, and how you might feel afterwards.</p><p class="article__blockquote"> <a href="https://confirmsubscription.com/h/i/DC735105D83847D9" target="_blank">For More Stories Like This, Sign Up for Our Newsletter</a></p><p>"Think about all the feelings that might make you want to join them. Are you worried about feeling left out of the group? Are you worried you might have less fun? Whatever it is, consider all the reasons you want to give up, and next time you are in that situation try to bring them readily to mind.</p> <p>Sadly, this doesnt quite work for me. It takes me about two hours before I cave and ask someone at the aforementioned gay bar for a cigarette. But I havent smoked in a while, and as the nicotine unpleasantly hits sober me, unaided by the boozy fugue I usually imbibe one in, Im kind of wondering why I even bothered in the first place. Maybe these cancerous tar sticks arebad? </p> <div class="ad-unit__container__container"><div class="article-iac__wrapper"></div></div><h2> Other (1 percent)</h2> <p>Only one percent of the British public has a resolution that doesnt fall into the previous nine Ive tried out, so heres mine: Im never doing another New Year's resolution again. Or, Im never going to try doing almost all of them at once because its impossible to effectively fulfill all of them at one go. Heres my advice: If you are keen on the idea of setting some 2019 goals, go easy on yourself, because you will fuck up. Dont set yourself impossible targets, like trying to go to the gym every day or swapping all your meals for macrobiotic bowls. Finally, congratulate yourself on actually making it to 2019you did good just surviving 2018. </p> <p>Oh! And go to the dentist. </p><p><i>This article originally appeared on VICE US.</i></p></div><div class="long-form-v2__after-body long-form-v2--center"><div class="article-after-body"><dl class="topics topic-list article-after-body__topics ff--accent lh--headline size--6 p-t-3--xs m-b-6--xs"><dt class="topic topic-list__title dsp-inline-block--xs m-b-0--xs">Tagged:</dt><dd class="topic topic-list__definition fw--bold dsp-inline-block--xs m-t-1--xs m-b-0--xs"><a class="topic__link bb--link" href="/en_asia/topic/health">Health</a></dd><dd class="topic topic-list__definition fw--bold dsp-inline-block--xs m-t-1--xs m-b-0--xs"><a class="topic__link bb--link" href="/en_asia/topic/uk">uk</a></dd><dd class="topic topic-list__definition fw--bold dsp-inline-block--xs m-t-1--xs m-b-0--xs"><a class="topic__link bb--link" href="/en_asia/topic/exercise">exercise</a></dd><dd class="topic topic-list__definition fw--bold dsp-inline-block--xs m-t-1--xs m-b-0--xs"><a class="topic__link bb--link" href="/en_asia/topic/new-years-resolutions">new year&#x27;s resolutions</a></dd><dd class="topic topic-list__definition fw--bold dsp-inline-block--xs m-t-1--xs m-b-0--xs"><a class="topic__link bb--link" href="/en_asia/topic/new-year-resolutions">new year resolutions</a></dd></dl></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></article></div></div><style jsx="true">
